We are trying to prove RH. Please read the attached latest draft.

Current status to assume:

* the direct provenance slice (\phi=Aq^{(7)}) is too universal on each generic block;
* finite-jet, finite-codimension, local pointwise, and same-tower differential attacks are exhausted;
* mixed local (4)-point theory is closed near the centered base.

Your task:

Look for the **first genuinely new canonical highest-new field** that is **not** in the differential algebra generated by
[
r(h)=q^{(7)}(h)
]
over the lower controlled coefficient field.

In other words, I want you to do a conceptual **new-generator audit** of the mixed/canonical package, not another direct-slice analysis.

Please try to answer:

* Is there a pointwise highest-new invariant whose leading content is not just a differential-algebraic function of (r)?
* If yes, can it be coupled pointwise to (r) or to (W^{[1]}) with nonzero determinant/rank?
* If no, can you prove a same-tower closure theorem for the currently available highest-new fields?

What to focus on:

* canonical/mixed fields above arbitrary quotient-septic geometry;
* provenance-sensitive fields that survive after mixed local closure;
* rank / generator analysis of highest-new slices.

Do not focus on:

* another theorem about arbitrary (\Delta_7);
* another local graph/bitangent argument;
* another attempt to derive a law for (\phi) from itself.

What I want back:

1. a list of the strongest candidate highest-new fields outside the current (q)-tower;
2. for each one, whether it is genuinely new or still same-tower;
3. the first plausible rank-(2) pointwise coupling, if any;
4. if everything stays same-tower, a clean theorem statement saying so.

The goal is a real new-generator finding, not edits.

Please prioritize checking whether that residue produces a highest-new field not in the differential tower generated by (r=q^{(7)}), or a rank-2 pointwise coupling involving (r), (W^{[1]}), or another external invariant.

1. Jet-module closure on the overlap patch

Here is the strongest abstract closure statement I see.
Proposition (highest-new jet-module closure).

Any currently explicit pointwise highest-new field on the overlap patch obtained from
x, Y, S
x, Y, S

by finitely many algebraic/rational operations, xx-derivatives, Wronskians, projectivizations, and finite jet extractions lies in the differential module

Why this is true.

\begin{remark}[Regularized source scalar for the mixed residual quotient]
\label{rem:regularized-source-scalar-mixed-residual}
In the notation of Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list},
write locally
\[
J_\lambda(x)=x^rA(x),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=x^rB(x),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0,
\]
and set
\[
Q(x):=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(x)}{J_\lambda(x)}.
\]
Then
\[
Q'(x)
=
\frac{J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'}{J_\lambda^2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
where
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
\]
is the source-level Wronskian from
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}.

Moreover, under the affine gauge change
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+\alpha c+\beta v_5+\gamma\lambda
\]
one has
\[
J_{u_5}\longmapsto J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda,
\qquad
Q\longmapsto Q+\gamma,
\]
so
\[
Q'(x)
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
is gauge-invariant. Thus, modulo the trivial additive constant in the
regularized ratio $Q$, the mixed residual quotient germ is already controlled
by the single scalar
\[
\mathcal D:=Q'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

On the nonmixed complement of $K_v=0$,
Remark~\ref{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point} give
\[
\mathcal D
=
\frac{M}{c^2}\,\mathcal R.
\]
So the exact fixed-shear residual lane is governed by the same regularized
source scalar already present on the nonmixed side, rather than by a second
primitive pointwise highest-new field.
\end{remark}

2) Insert immediately after Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}

This is the main structural compression: quotient transport scalar, residual ladder, odd source-Wronskian order.

\begin{proposition}[Quotient transport scalar and residual ladder on the exact fixed-shear $K_v=0$ slice]
\label{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}
Assume the additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane from
Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}. Let
\[
r:=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\qquad
q:=\ord_0J_{u_5},
\]
and write in the centered involutive source coordinate $t$
\[
J_\lambda(t)=t^rA(t),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(t)=t^rB(t),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0.
\]
Set
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}.
\]
Then the following hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item $Q$ is even:
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t).
\]
Hence there exists a unique analytic germ $\widehat Q$ in
\[
u:=t^2
\]
such that
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]

\item If
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
then
\[
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}
=
Q'(t)
=
2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)
=
2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

\item If
\[
e:=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}\in\mathbf Z_{\ge 0},
\]
then
\[
q-r=2e+2,
\qquad
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=r+2e+4,
\]
and
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]

\item In particular,
\[
r\ \text{is even},
\qquad
q-r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 2},
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\ \text{is odd}.
\]
So the exact fixed-shear residual lane lies on an even-support ladder over
$K_v=0$, while the associated source-level Wronskian vanishes to odd order.

\item The currently surviving quartic--sextic residual model is exactly the
first rung of this ladder:
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)
\iff
(r,e)=(2,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}, the
projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},
\qquad
G(-t)=G(t).
\]
Thus the quotient-diagonal mixed residue is even/even, so the regularized ratio
$Q=B/A$ is even, giving the factorization
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Differentiating yields
\[
Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
On the other hand,
Remark~\ref{rem:regularized-source-scalar-mixed-residual} gives
\[
Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}.
\]
Since
\[
J_\lambda(t)^2=t^{2r}A(t)^2,
\]
this gives
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)
=
2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
If $e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}$, then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
so
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2}.
\]
Hence
\[
q-r=\ord_0(Q(t)-Q(0))=2e+2.
\]
Now
Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list} gives
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=q+2,
\]
so
\[
n=r+2e+4.
\]
Also
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]
Since $m$ is even, $r=m-2$ is even. The final statements follow immediately.
\end{proof}

3) Insert immediately after Proposition~\ref{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}

This captures the quartic‚Äìsextic goodies and the local no-reentry statement.

\begin{corollary}[Quartic--sextic quotient injectivity and local no-reentry]
\label{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry}
Assume the quartic--sextic residual case
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]
Then
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}u+O(u^2),
\]
so
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac12\left(\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}\right)'(0)
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
\]

Hence $\widehat Q$ is a local analytic diffeomorphism in the quotient variable
$u=t^2$. In particular, after quotienting the involution
$t\leftrightarrow -t$, there is no local exact fixed-shear re-entry: every
nearby fixed-shear level is attained by at most one quotient point.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
In the quartic--sextic case, Proposition~\ref{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}
gives
\[
(r,e)=(2,0).
\]
So $\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0$, which is exactly the displayed coefficient
$\kappa_{2,2}$. The explicit formulas follow from
Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list} and the identity
\[
Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
Since
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0,
\]
the analytic inverse function theorem implies that $\widehat Q$ is a local
diffeomorphism in $u=t^2$.
\end{proof}

4) Insert immediately after Theorem~\ref{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero}

This is the clean one-sided exclusion theorem for H3H3‚Äã, and it sharpens the local 33-point picture.

\begin{corollary}[One-sided exclusion for repeated-node tangent contact]
\label{cor:one-sided-exclusion-repeated-node-tangent-contact}
Under the hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero},
there exists $\varepsilon>0$ such that
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0
\]
for every same-side pair with
\[
-\varepsilon<a<u<0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
0<a<u<\varepsilon.
\]
Equivalently, every sufficiently small off-diagonal solution of
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
is necessarily opposite-side.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Using
\[
H_3(a,u)=S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a),
\]
one has the exact integral identity
\[
H_3(a,u)=\int_a^u (u-t)\,S''(t)\,dt.
\]
Since $x=0$ is an isolated finite-order zero of $K_v=(x')^3S''$ on a good
$v_5$-patch, the analytic function $S''$ has constant nonzero sign on each
punctured one-sided interval
\[
(-\varepsilon,0),
\qquad
(0,\varepsilon)
\]
after shrinking. If $a<u$ lie on the same side of $0$, then
\[
u-t>0
\]
for all $t\in(a,u)$, and $S''(t)$ has fixed nonzero sign on the whole interval.
So the integrand has fixed nonzero sign, and therefore
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

This gives you, implicitly, the useful consequence that the local opposite-side classification theorem is actually exhaustive for sufficiently small off-diagonal H3H3‚Äã-branches.

Sure! Here's a concise summary of the three major updates, ready to share with your teammates:

---

### **Summary of Recent Updates to the Paper**

#### **1. Reduced Quotient-Cusp Lane to Critical-Value Ordering Problem**

* **Key Change**: The residual quotient-cusp lane has been reduced to a **critical-value ordering problem** for the transport scalar (\widehat{\mathcal D}). This allows us to focus solely on proving a **no-reentry** or **critical-value separation** theorem.
* **Main Result**: The previous complex quotient-cusp geometry has collapsed into a **finite critical-value separation problem**, where we now only need to prove that the critical values of (\widehat Q) (and by extension (\widehat{\mathcal D})) follow a strict ordering with no inverted intervals.
* **Impact**: This update simplifies the entire attack, focusing it entirely on the ordering of critical values.

---

#### **2. Local No-Reentry and Global Critical-Value Problem**

* **Key Change**: The previous attack on the **Jensen gap/recurrence** mechanisms has been superseded by a focus on **no-reentry** principles for the quotient residual. We now treat the **gap-rank monotonicity** and **persistence pairing** problem.
* **Main Result**: The residual lane has been reduced to a **finite sequence of non-overlapping intervals**, each determined by the **critical-value ordering**. We now need to prove that there are no **overlapping intervals** for the quotient transport scalar (\widehat{\mathcal D}) along the quotient branch.
* **Impact**: This shifts our focus away from the earlier excursion-chain-based models to a global, **monotone** argument based on **gap-function ordering** and persistence.

---

#### **3. Exact Scalar (\widehat{\mathcal D}) and Quotient Transport Theory**

* **Key Change**: The focus has shifted from analyzing the derivative geometry of (M_1) to focusing on the **quotient transport scalar (\widehat{\mathcal D})** (and its associated function (\widehat Q)).
* **Main Result**: The scalar (\widehat{\mathcal D}) and its gap function now serve as the **canonical transport object** to analyze. The residual quotient-cusp problem is now exactly about proving that **(\widehat Q)** satisfies a **non-intersection condition** and can never have **overlapping zero crossings** along the quotient branch.
* **Impact**: This simplifies the residual quotient-cusp lane by focusing solely on the behavior of (\widehat Q), using **gap-function analysis** to determine whether or not an inversion occurs.

---

### **Conclusion**

These three updates represent a **major simplification** in the attack on the quotient-cusp residual lane. By reducing the problem to a critical-value ordering and gap-function monotonicity analysis for (\widehat{\mathcal D}), we now have a clearer path to closing the lane. The next steps will involve proving the **global monotonicity** of these functions and ensuring that no overlapping zero crossings occur, which will ultimately close the lane.

This turns the residual exact fixed-shear recurrence problem into a much more rigid combinatorial one:

    one fixed level Œ≥Œ≥ can only recur by visiting successive RR-sign chambers, one hit per chamber.

That is a real strengthening.
Bridge to the fixed-Œ≥Œ≥ nonrecurrence package

This also sharpens the earlier reduction to the fixed-Œ≥Œ≥ sheared 33-point branches.

Each regular hit of Q=Œ≥Q=Œ≥ is a simple odd zero of JŒ≥JŒ≥‚Äã, so by the fixed-Œ≥Œ≥ theorem it seeds a unique maximal opposite-side sheared 33-point branch segment. The chamber-separation theorem above now says those births must occur in different RR-sign chambers, at most one birth per chamber.

So a regular mm-fold return of one exact fixed-shear level Œ≥Œ≥ forces:

    mm distinct odd zeros of JŒ≥JŒ≥‚Äã,

    each in a different RR-sign chamber,

That is much tighter than the earlier ‚Äúmulti-birth chamber-concatenation‚Äù statement.

The honest limit

    no skipping the odd-zero chamber structure,

    one hit per chamber at most.

That is where the attack now lands.

2. Proof sketch

This is standard 1D Morse/Reeb behavior, but in our setting it is useful to spell it out.

For any regular level ŒªŒª, every bounded component of {Q^>Œª}{Q
‚Äã>Œª} is an interval whose boundary points are level hits. Between two nearby levels with no critical values in between, the topology of the superlevel set cannot change because Q^‚Ä≤‚âÝ0Q
‚Äã‚Ä≤ÓÄÝ=0 on every boundary hit, so the endpoints move smoothly.

The only times the component structure can change are when ŒªŒª crosses a critical value. For a superlevel set, only local minima matter:

    crossing a local maximum just creates or removes a tiny visible island near that maximum,

    crossing a local minimum merges the two adjacent superlevel components into one.

Since the line is ordered, the merge is automatically adjacent and binary. Iterating this from high level down to Œ≥Œ≥ yields the whole island.

The sublevel case is identical with maxima/minima interchanged.

Five odd critical points

Exactly two adjacent binary mergers in succession.

And so on.

So the earlier reductions were not isolated special cases. They are the first nodes of the same general merge tree.

19. Discrete-state rigidity on regular families

A final strong reduction came from observing:

    regular excursion families are connected analytic families;

    the downstream finite-core / defect-gate state is naturally discrete/combinatorial.

Therefore any such discrete downstream state is automatically constant on each connected regular excursion family.

So regular transport edges carry no internal state changes at all.

Thus the only remaining possible hiddenness is concentrated at the discrete odd-merger / tie vertices.

This is probably the cleanest regular-to-finite-core bridge obtained in the whole attack.
20. Negative findings / what failed / honest boundaries

(a) No second pointwise generator

(b) No direct exclusion of critical-value oscillation

    ‚Äã,

(c) No direct proof that hidden-reset islands cannot occur

We progressively demoted the apparent first hidden-reset cases:

    one critical point: harmless,

    three-extrema island: still visible,

    tie case: not a new first-order loophole.

But we did not prove that no more complicated hidden regular reset can occur purely from the current local identities.
(d) No proof yet of local downstream update uniqueness

This is now the exact bottleneck:

uniqueness/coherence of the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state at one odd-critical merger (and tie).‚Äã

Everything else on the regular side has been reduced away.
